Objection to Perception and the View of Suspension
Sanusi presents an objection based on necessary connection with contact and argues for suspension of judgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why some scholars denied Allah's perception of smells, tastes, and tangible things, and why the correct position is one of suspension due to lack of clear scriptural evidence.

Core Idea
Perception does not necessitate physical contact; suspension is warranted when evidence is absent.

This passage from Sanusi's commentary addresses a specific objection against affirming certain sensory perceptions for Allah. Some scholars argued that perceiving smells, tastes, and tangible things requires physical contact, which cannot apply to Allah. Sanusi rejects that rational link and then presents the position of suspension (waqf) as the most prudent stance. Let's follow his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the flow from objection to refutation to suspension.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the denier's argument
Find where Sanusi presents the argument that perception necessitates contact. How does he characterize this belief?
Look for the phrase 'لما رآه ملزوماً للاتصال'.
3
Understand Sanusi's rebuttal
Sanusi says perception does not necessitate contact. What distinction does he make between custom and reason?
He says contact is a condition by custom, not by reason.
4
Grasp the suspension position
Sanusi presents suspension (الوقف) as the verified view. Why do al-Muqattirih and Ibn al-Tilmisani adopt this?
Their method relies on scriptural evidence, which is lacking here.
5
Reflect on the method
Consider the broader principle: in matters of divine attributes, what should guide our affirmation or negation?
The passage emphasizes reliance on revealed sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما اعتقد بعض العلماء الملازمة العقليَّةَ بين الإدراكِ وبينَها ، أو إيهام ذلكَ .. منع أيضاً إثبات هذه الإدراكاتِ له جلَّ وعلا ، وجعلَ الإحاطة بمتعلقاتِها داخلاً في علمِهِ تعالى ، وإلى هذا القول أشرتُ بقولي : ( وجزم بعضُهم بنفيهِ ) أي : بنفي الإدراك المتعلقِ بالمشمومات والمذوقاتِ والملموساتِ ؛ يعني : ويُستغنى عنه بالعلم ، وقولي : ( لما رآه ملزوماً للاتصال ) هذهِ حُجَّةُ النافي . وقوله : ( والحقُّ : أَنَّهُ لا يستلزمُهُ ) أي : الإدراك لا يستلزم الاتصال بالأجسام ؛ لما عرفتَ أنَّ الإدراك أمر وراء الاتصال والاتصال شرط فيه بالنسبة إلينا عادةً لا عقلاً . وقولي : ( والتحقيقُ فيهِ : الوقفُ ) أي : في الإدراك ؛ بمعنى : أهو ثابت له تعالى زائد على علمه أم لا ، فيُترَكُ الجزم بأحدِ الأمرين لعدم ظهورِ دليلهِ ، وهذا القولُ مختارُ المقترح وابن التلمساني ، وحُجَّتُهما : ما أشرنا إليه بعد ؛ وهو أنَّ التحقيق عندهما في نفي النقائص الاعتماد على دليل السمع ، وقد ثبت في السمع والبصر والكلام كما قدمناه فيها ، ولم يثبت في هذا الإدراكِ ، فوجبَ الوقفُ عن إثباتِهِ ونفيه .
And when some scholars believed in the rational concomitance between perception and them [the sensory acts], or the illusion of that, they also prohibited affirming these perceptions for Him, exalted, and made encompassing their objects part of His knowledge, exalted. And to this statement I alluded by my saying: 'And some of them decisively affirmed its negation,' i.e., the negation of perception related to smells, tastes, and tangible things; meaning: one dispenses with it through knowledge. And my saying: 'because he saw it as necessitating contact'—this is the argument of the denier. And his saying: 'The truth is that it does not necessitate it,' i.e., perception does not necessitate contact with bodies; because you have known that perception is beyond contact and contact is a condition for it with respect to us customarily, not rationally. And my saying: 'And the verification in it is suspension,' i.e., regarding perception; meaning: whether it is affirmed for Him, exalted, in addition to His knowledge or not, so one refrains from deciding either of the two matters due to lack of evidence for it. And this statement is the choice of al-Muqattirih and Ibn al-Tilmisani, and their proof is what we alluded to later: that verification in negating deficiencies in their view relies on scriptural evidence, and it has been established for hearing, sight, and speech as we have presented concerning them, but it has not been established for this perception, so suspension regarding its affirmation and negation became necessary.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage presents the objection to affirming Allah's perception of smells, tastes, and tangible things, and then gives the author's preferred position of suspension (waqf). The objection is from those scholars who believed there is a rational necessary connection (لازمة عقلية) between such perception and physical contact (الاتصال بالأجسام). Because of this, or even the illusion of it, they denied that Allah possesses such perceptions and instead subsumed the knowledge of those objects under His absolute knowledge. The author notes that he alluded to this view earlier with his statement 'And some of them decisively affirmed its negation.' The denier's argument is that perception necessitates contact, which is impossible for Allah. However, the correct view (الحق) is that perception does not necessitate contact, because contact is a condition for perception only by custom (عادة), not by reason (عقلاً). Then the author presents the position of verification (التحقيق) as suspension (الوقف). This suspension means to refrain from affirming or denying that Allah has this perception as an attribute additional to His knowledge, due to the lack of clear evidence (دليل). The scholars al-Muqattirih and Ibn al-Tilmisani hold this view. Their proof is that in negating deficiencies from Allah, one should rely on scriptural evidence (السمع). For hearing, sight, and speech, scriptural evidence established them as attributes, but for this perception, no such scriptural evidence is found, so one must suspend judgment—neither affirm nor deny it.

Key Terms
الملازمة العقلية
الاتصال
النافي
الوقف
السمع
التحقيق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Suspension (waqf) implies rejecting the attribute of perception for Allah.
Correction: Suspension is a position of withholding judgment due to lack of evidence, not a rejection. It means neither affirming nor denying the attribute as additional to knowledge.

Checkpoint
Why do al-Muqattirih and Ibn al-Tilmisani adopt the position of suspension (waqf) regarding this perception?
A) Because they believe perception necessitates contact
B) Because scriptural evidence is lacking for this perception
C) Because they deny all additional attributes
D) Because they follow the rational proof

Key Takeaway
When scriptural evidence does not clearly affirm or deny an attribute, suspension of judgment is the prudent course, avoiding both rejection and unwarranted affirmation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Your mind naturally assumes that perception requires physical contact, as the deniers did. What other assumptions about Allah have you inherited from the created world without realizing? How will you actively distinguish between customary patterns and rational necessity when thinking about the Divine?
?
The scholars suspended judgment because the evidence was not there. Is there an area of your religious practice or belief where you are holding a strong opinion despite lacking clear evidence? Are you willing to let go of that certainty and adopt the humble position of 'I do not know'?

The Position of Refraining Regarding Divine Perception
Sanusi explains the dispute over perception and upholds the position of refraining.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate about divine perception and the methodological reasoning behind refraining (al-waqf) from affirming or negating an additional attribute.

Core Idea
Refraining is not denial; it is intellectual humility in the absence of decisive revelation.

Sanusi here tackles a subtle question: does Allah have a separate attribute of perception beyond His knowledge? Some scholars argued that perception implies physical contact, so they reduced it to knowledge. Others saw that connection is only human custom, not a logical necessity. Sanusi presents the position of refraining, based on the principle that for matters of divine attributes, we rely on transmitted proof only when clear.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic carefully to follow Sanusi's layered discussion. Note how he presents the opinion of those who deny perception and his rebuttal.
2
Identify the key claims
Find where Sanusi states the truth (al-haqq) and the verification (al-tahqīq) about perception. Notice the distinction between intellectual and customary conditions.
3
Understand refraining (al-waqf)
Refraining means suspending judgment. Why is it justified here? Look at the proof from transmitted revelation and why it doesn't settle the matter for perception.
This connects to broader Ash'ari methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإدراك غيرَ زائد عليها لكان هذا اللفظ متناقضاً . ولما اعتقد بعض العلماء الملازمة العقليَّةَ بين الإدراكِ وبينَها ، أو إيهام ذلكَ .. منع أيضاً إثبات هذه الإدراكاتِ له جلَّ وعلا ، وجعلَ الإحاطة بمتعلقاتِها داخلاً في علمِهِ تعالى ، وإلى هذا القول أشرتُ بقولي : ( وجزم بعضُهم بنفيهِ ) أي : بنفي الإدراك المتعلقِ بالمشمومات والمذوقاتِ والملموساتِ ؛ يعني : ويُستغنى عنه بالعلم ، وقولي : ( لما رآه ملزوماً للاتصال ) هذهِ حُجَّةُ النافي . وقوله : ( والحقُّ : أَنَّهُ لا يستلزمُهُ ) أي : الإدراك لا يستلزم الاتصال بالأجسام ؛ لما عرفتَ أنَّ الإدراك أمر وراء الاتصال والاتصال شرط فيه بالنسبة إلينا عادةً لا عقلاً . وقولي : ( والتحقيقُ فيهِ : الوقفُ ) أي : في الإدراك ؛ بمعنى : أهو ثابت له تعالى زائد على علمه أم لا ، فيُترَكُ الجزم بأحدِ الأمرين لعدم ظهورِ دليلهِ ، وهذا القولُ مختارُ المقترح وابن التلمساني ، وحُجَّتُهما : ما أشرنا إليه بعد ؛ وهو أنَّ التحقيق عندهما في نفي النقائص الاعتماد على دليل السمع ، وقد ثبت في السمع والبصر والكلام كما قدمناه فيها ، ولم يثبت في هذا الإدراكِ ، فوجبَ الوقفُ عن إثباتِهِ ونفيهِ .
If perception were not additional to them, then this expression would be contradictory. And when some scholars believed in the intellectual entailment between perception and them, or the suggestion of that, they also prevented affirming these perceptions for Him, Exalted and Glorified, and made the encompassing of their objects included in His knowledge, may He be Exalted. And to this statement I alluded with my saying: 'And some of them firmly asserted its negation' i.e., the negation of perception related to smells, tastes, and touches; meaning: and it is dispensed with by knowledge. And my saying: 'Because he saw it as necessarily requiring connection'—this is the proof of the negator. And his saying: 'And the truth is that it does not necessitate it' i.e., perception does not necessitate connection to bodies; because you have known that perception is something beyond connection, and connection is a condition for it with respect to us customarily, not intellectually. And my saying: 'And the verification concerning it is refraining' i.e., concerning perception; meaning: whether it is established for Him, Exalted, as additional to His knowledge or not, so one refrains from asserting either of the two matters due to the lack of clarity of its proof. This is the chosen view of al-Muqri' and Ibn al-Tilmisani, and their proof: what we have indicated after; which is that verification according to them in negating deficiencies relies on evidence from transmitted revelation (al-sam'), and it has been established for hearing, sight, and speech as we have presented concerning them, but it has not been established for this perception, so refraining from affirming or negating it becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the divine attribute of perception (al-idrāk) and the controversy surrounding it. The author begins by stating a conditional: if perception were not additional to the other attributes, the term would be contradictory. He then explains that some scholars believed perception necessarily entails physical connection to bodies, leading them to deny perception for smells, tastes, and touches, instead subsuming those under knowledge. The author clarifies that the truth is perception does not necessitate connection; connection is only a customary condition for humans, not an intellectual requirement. He then presents the position of refraining (al-waqf): we cannot definitively affirm or deny that perception is an additional attribute because the proof from transmitted revelation (al-sam') is not clear. He cites al-Muqri' and Ibn al-Tilmisani as holding this view, arguing that since hearing, sight, and speech are affirmed by revelation but perception is not, we must suspend judgment. Thus, the passage defends the methodology of relying on revelation for affirming attributes and shows the limits of rational inference.

Key Terms
الإدراك
الملازمة العقلية
الاتصال
الوقف
السمع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Refraining is equivalent to denying the attribute.
Correction: Refraining means suspending judgment, not negation, due to insufficient evidence.

Checkpoint
Why do some scholars refrain from affirming or negating perception as a separate divine attribute?
A) Because it entails connection to bodies.
B) Because there is no clear evidence from transmitted revelation (al-sam').
C) Because it is included in divine knowledge.
D) Because the intellect cannot grasp it.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi defends refraining (al-waqf) regarding divine perception because the revealed evidence does not clearly support affirming or negating it as an additional attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there areas of your faith where you have been too quick to affirm or deny something about Allah without clear evidence? Will you now adopt the posture of refraining until decisive revelation comes?
?
Do you ever assume that Allah must be like His creation because your experience is limited? How can this lesson on perception and connection free you from that assumption and deepen your tawheed?
?
Refraining (al-waqf) requires intellectual humility. Is there a belief about Allah that you cling to stubbornly without textual support? Will you examine it and choose to refrain where proof is absent?

Establishing the Seven Attributes of Meanings
Sanusi establishes the necessity of seven attributes of meanings from the seven divine descriptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the seven divine descriptions (powerful, willing, etc.) necessarily imply real attributes (power, will, etc.) that subsist in Allah's essence, and why perception and the attributes of eternality are treated separately.

Core Idea
The seven attributes of meanings are real entities in the divine essence, distinct from the descriptions.

This passage opens a crucial chapter in Sanusi's creed. It establishes that when we say Allah is powerful, willing, knowing, etc., these are not mere names but have corresponding real attributes that exist in His essence. Sanusi also clarifies why the eighth description of perception is disputed and why the attributes of being ancient and everlasting are handled earlier. Let's explore this foundational doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the literal translation. Notice the compressed style and the author's precise language.
Pay attention to the terms 'صفات المعاني' and 'الأوصاف السبع'.
2
Identify the seven descriptions and their attributes
The passage states that the seven descriptions (e.g., qādir, murīd) are accompanied by meanings (qudra, irāda). List the seven from the text.
The seven are: power, will, knowledge, life, hearing, sight, speech.
3
Note the exclusion of perception
Sanusi explains why the eighth description (being perceiving) is not included. Find the reason and understand the concept of refraining (al-waqf).
Disagreement and lack of clear proof led to excluding it.
4
Understand the status of ancient and everlasting
The passage mentions that the attributes of being ancient and everlasting have already been discussed. This clarifies that they are not part of the seven attributes of meanings.
They are separate from the seven.

Chapter on establishing the attributes of meanings and their entailment of the attributes of being described [with those attributes]. Then we say: It is necessarily required that these seven descriptions are accompanied by meanings subsisting in His Essence, so that He is powerful (qādir) by power (qudra), willing (murīd) by will (irāda), and likewise up to the last of them. He means by the seven descriptions: what was mentioned before of His being Powerful... to Speaking, and indeed he did not count them as eight by adding His being Perceiving (mudrik) because of the disagreement concerning this eighth attribute, and because it was transmitted that the verification concerning it is refraining (al-waqf). As for His being Ancient (qadīm) and Everlasting (bāqī): it has preceded what concerns their entailment of the attributes of eternality (qidam) and permanence (baqā'). And know: that these seven attributes whose proof of establishment has been completed are called
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a formal chapter opening that introduces the doctrine of the attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī). It begins by stating the necessary conclusion: the seven descriptions (power, will, knowledge, life, hearing, sight, speech) must have corresponding real attributes that subsist in the divine Essence. The author then clarifies that these seven descriptions are those previously listed, and he explicitly excludes an eighth—perception—due to the controversy and the earlier conclusion of refraining. He also notes that the attributes of being ancient and everlasting are handled separately earlier. The passage ends incompletely but identifies that these seven attributes are called something (likely 'attributes of meanings'). The key point is that the attributes are additional to the essence and are proven by rational necessity from the descriptions.

Correction: The descriptions are not the attributes; rather, each description (e.g., qādir) entails a distinct attribute (qudra) that subsists in the essence.

The Attributes of Meanings and Their Causal Role
Sanusi defines ṣifāt al-maʿānī as causes of the meaningful attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between the attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī) as causes and the meaningful attributes (ṣifāt maʿnawiyya) as their effects, and why this distinction is important in Ashʿarī theology.

Core Idea
Attributes of meanings are the causes; meaningful attributes are the effects.

After establishing the seven essential attributes of God, Sanusi now introduces a crucial distinction: these attributes are not merely names; they are caused by real meanings that subsist in God’s essence. This passage clarifies the causal relationship between what he calls 'attributes of meanings' and the resulting 'meaningful attributes.' Understanding this will help you see how Ashʿarī theologians think about God’s attributes as real and distinct from His essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi uses a very logical and sequential style here.
2
Identify the seven attributes and the omitted eighth
The passage lists seven attributes: power, will, knowledge, life, hearing, sight, speech. Note that perception is omitted due to disagreement. Observe how this sets the stage for the causal discussion.
The eighth attribute of perception is disputed among scholars.
3
Understand the causal relationship
Focus on the definitions: ṣifāt al-maʿānī are the causes (e.g., power is a cause), while ṣifāt maʿnawiyya are the effects (e.g., being powerful). See how the passage explicitly states this cause-effect link.
The meaningful attributes are 'caused' by the attributes of meanings.
4
Contrast with common misconceptions
Review the common misunderstanding that the two categories are the same. The passage clarifies they are distinct: causes vs. effects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصلُ في إثباتِ صفاتِ المعاني ، وملازمتها للمعنوية . ثم نقول : يتعيَّنُ أنْ تكون هذه الأوصافُ السبع تلازمها معانٍ تقوم بذاتِهِ تعالى ، فيكون قادراً بقدرة ، مريداً بإرادة ، ثم كذلك إلى آخرها . يعني بالأوصافِ السبع : ما ذكرَ قبلُ مِنْ كونه تعالى قادراً ... إلى متكلماً ، وإنَّما لم يَعُدَّها ثمانياً بزيادة كونِهِ مُدْرِكاً ؛ لما رأى مِنَ التنازعِ في هذهِ الصفة الثامنة ، ولما نقلَ أنَّ التحقيق فيها الوقف . وأما كونه قديماً وباقياً : فقد تقدَّمَ ما في ملازمتِهما لصفتي القدمِ والبقاء . واعلم : أنَّ هذه الصفاتِ السبعَ التي فرغَ مِنْ برهان ثبوتِها تُسمَّى لأجل ملازمتها معاني أَخرَ هي عِلَلٌ لـ : صفاتٍ معنويةً ، وأحوالاً معنوية ، نُسِبَتْ إلى المعاني التي هي عِللها؛ ككونه قادراً عليه القدرة، وككونه عالماً علتُهُ العلم ، وهكذا إلى آخرِها ، وتُسمَّى هذهِ العِلَلُ الملازمة للمعنويَّةِ : صفاتِ المعاني ، فالمعنوية : صفات ثابتة للذاتِ مُعلَّلَةٌ بمعنى قائم بالذاتِ ، وعللها صفات لا تتصفُ بوجود ولا عدم، موجودة قائمة بالذاتِ مُوجِبةٌ لها حُكْماً ؛ وهو تلك الصفة المعنوية .
Chapter on establishing the attributes of meanings and their accompaniment to the meaningful. Then we say: It is determined that these seven descriptions are accompanied by meanings subsisting in His Essence, Exalted, so that He is powerful by power, willing by will, and likewise to the end. He means by the seven descriptions: what was previously mentioned of His being powerful... to speaking. And he did not count them as eight by adding His being perceptive, because he saw the dispute about this eighth attribute, and because it was narrated that the definitive reality regarding it is suspension. As for His being pre-eternal and everlasting: what has preceded regarding their accompaniment to the attributes of pre-eternity and everlastingness. Know that these seven attributes, whose proof of existence has been completed, are called, because they are accompanied by other meanings that are causes for meaningful attributes and meaningful states, attributed to the meanings which are their causes; such as His being powerful is caused by power, and His being knowing is caused by knowledge, and so on to the end. And these causes that accompany the meaningful are called 'attributes of meanings'. So the meaningful are attributes established for the Essence that are caused by a meaning subsisting in the Essence, and their causes are attributes that are not described by existence or non-existence, existing, subsisting in the Essence, necessitating for it a judgment; and that judgment is that meaningful attribute.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage defines the 'attributes of meanings' (ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī) and clarifies their relationship to the 'meaningful attributes' (ṣifāt ma‘nawiyya). The author states that the seven essential attributes (power, will, knowledge, life, hearing, sight, speech) are necessarily accompanied by meanings that subsist in God's essence. For example, being powerful entails a meaning called 'power', being willing entails 'will', etc. He notes that the eighth attribute of perception is omitted because of disagreement. Then he clarifies naming: these seven attributes are called 'attributes of meanings' because they are accompanied by other meanings that are causes for the meaningful attributes and meaningful states. These causes are the attributes of meanings; they are not described by existence or non-existence but are existing in the essence and necessitate a judgment, which is the meaningful attribute. The meaningful attributes are those that are caused, while the attributes of meanings are the causes.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the attributes of meanings and the meaningful attributes are the same category.
Correction: They are distinct: attributes of meanings are the causes (e.g., power), while meaningful attributes are the effects (e.g., being powerful).

D) They are unrelated.

Key Takeaway
The seven essential attributes are accompanied by meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī) which are the causes for the meaningful attributes (ṣifāt maʿnawiyya).

For example, do you assume that doing good deeds makes you good, rather than that goodness is a root in your soul? How does this insight from kalam challenge your self-perception?

Two Views on the Intermediary Between Existence and Non-existence
Sanusi contrasts two positions on the validity of an intermediary between existence and non-existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two theological positions on the validity of an intermediary category between existence and non-existence and how this affects the concept of divine attributes.

Core Idea
Whether a state can exist between existence and non-existence determines the reality of divine attributes.

Sanusi presents a crucial juncture in kalam: the status of states (ahwal). The previous discussion on ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī assumed an intermediary category. But there is an opposing view that rejects any intermediary, limiting reality to essence and existential attributes. This passage compares both positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the two conditional statements. Notice the structure: 'All of this is according to... But according to...'
The passage directly contrasts two views using the phrase 'هذا كله على القول... وأما على القول'.
2
Identify the two positions
Identify that the first position accepts an intermediary (wāsita) between existence and non-existence, while the second denies it. Determine what each position affirms or denies regarding attributes and states.
3
Understand the implications for divine attributes
Reflect on how the acceptance of an intermediary allows for the concept of states (ahwal) like being knowing or powerful as distinct from existential attributes. The denial reduces everything to essence and existential attributes only.
This connects to the broader debate on God's attributes in Ash‘arī theology.
4
Reflect on theological significance
Consider why this distinction matters. The acceptance or rejection of states affects how we describe God's attributes and the relationship between essence and attributes.
This lesson sets the stage for understanding the doctrine of ahwal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا كله على القول بصحة الواسطة بين الوجود والعدم . وأما على القول بنفيها : فليسَ ثَمَّ إلا الذات وصفات المعاني الوجودية ، ولا معنى عندهم لكونه عالماً أو قادراً إلا قيام العلم والقدرةِ بهِ ، فلا حالَ عند هؤلاء لا معنويةً ولا نفسيَّةً
All of this is according to the opinion that the intermediary between existence and non-existence is valid. But according to the opinion denying it: there is nothing other than the essence and the existential attributes of meanings, and there is no meaning for them in His being knowing or powerful except the subsistence of knowledge and power in Him, so there is no state according to these, neither meaningful nor psychic.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage presents two positions on the existence of states (ahwal). The previous discussion about ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī being descriptions that are not existence nor non-existence is based on the view that an intermediary (wāsita) between existence and non-existence is valid. That is, some theologians (like the Ash‘arīs who accept ahwal) hold that there are attributes that are neither existent nor non-existent but are 'states'. The alternative view, which denies such an intermediary, holds that only the essence and the existential attributes of meanings (like knowledge and power as actual entities) exist. According to this view, there is no state (ḥāl) at all, neither meaningful (ma‘nawiyya) nor psychic (nafsiyya). Thus, the concept of a state as a separate category is rejected.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that acceptance of states (ahwal) is universally agreed upon in Ash‘arī theology.
Correction: This passage shows that acceptance of ahwal depends on the prior acceptance of an intermediary category between existence and non-existence, which is a contested position.

Checkpoint

D) The essence and the states exist.

Key Takeaway
The existence of states (ahwal) depends on the acceptance of an intermediary category between existence and non-existence.

?
The denial of ahwal reduces 'being knowing' to merely the subsistence of knowledge. Does this feel less personal to you? How does this affect your relationship with a God whose attributes are not additional realities? Challenge yourself to praise Him without needing to imagine extra layers.

The Two Schools on States and the Threefold Classification of Attributes
Sanusi divides theologians into two schools on states and explains the threefold attribute classification for the affirmers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the division of theologians regarding the reality of states (ahwal) and how this leads to different classifications of divine attributes.

Core Idea
Theologians split on whether states are real; this shapes their attribute classifications.

This passage from Sanusi's Umm al-Barahin lays out a foundational disagreement in kalam: are divine attributes best understood as states (ahwal) or as meanings? Sanusi first presents the two camps—those who deny states (led by al-Ash'ari) and those who affirm them (like al-Qadi and Imam al-Haramayn). Then, for the affirmers, he explains how attributes are divided into three kinds: psychic, meaningful, and meanings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups of theologians
Read the opening sentence carefully to find the two groups regarding states (ahwal). Note that one group denies states and the other affirms them.
The passage states that al-Ash'ari and many investigators deny states, while al-Qadi and Imam al-Haramayn affirm them.
2
Understand the definition of 'state' (al-hal)
Look at Sanusi's definition: a state is a positive attribute that is not described by existence or non-existence. Reflect on what this means—it is a real attribute that is neither existent nor non-existent in the usual sense.
This definition is crucial for understanding the debate.
3
See the consequences of each position
Note that for deniers, only 'attributes of meanings' (sifat al-ma'ani) exist. For affirmers, attributes are divided into three kinds. Understand how each school's view shapes its classification.
The passage explicitly states the consequence for each group.
4
Examine the threefold division for affirmers
For those who affirm states, attributes are three: psychic (nafsiyya), meaningful (ma'nawiyya), and meanings (ma'ani). With the aid of the commentary, understand the reasoning: what is actualized is either by itself (the existent attribute like knowledge) or by something else (the state).
The reason for exclusivity (hierarchical division) is explained in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالجملة : فالمتكلمون على فريقين : فريق ينفي الحال ، وفريق يثبتها . وحقيقةُ الحالِ : صفةً إثباتٍ لا تتصف بالوجود ولا بالعدم . فالقائلون بنفي الأحوالِ ؛ كالشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري وكثير مِنَ المحققين : ليس عندهم مِنَ الصفاتِ إلا صفات المعاني . والقائلون بثبوتِ الحالِ ؛ كالقاضي وإمام الحرمين : يقسمونَ الصفات ثلاثة أقسام : نفسيَّةٌ ، ومعنوية ، ومعانٍ . ووجه الحصر : : أنَّ المتحقَّقَ إِمَّا أَنْ يتحقَّقَ باعتبارِ نفسِهِ ، أو باعتبار غيرِه . الأول : الموجود (أي : الوصف الموجود؛ كالعلم والقدرة مثلاً. «عكاري» (ق145))، والثاني : الحالُ؛ وهو إما أنْ يكونَ الغيرُ الذي تحقَّقَ بهِ .
In summary: The theologians are two groups: a group that denies the state, and a group that affirms it. The reality of the state is: a positive attribute that is not described by existence or non-existence. So those who deny states, like Shaykh Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ash‘arī and many of the investigators, have no attributes except attributes of meanings. Those who affirm the state, like al-Qāḍī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn, divide the attributes into three kinds: psychic, meaningful, and meanings. The reason for the exclusivity is: what is actualized is either actualized by consideration of itself or by consideration of something else. The first is the existent (meaning the existing description; like knowledge and power, for example. ‘Akari, folio 145), and the second is the state; and it is either that the something else by which it is actualized...
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage presents a classification of theologians based on their stance on the reality of states (ahwal). Two groups: those who deny states (like al-Ash‘arī and many scholars) and those who affirm them (like al-Qāḍī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn). The definition of a state is given: an affirmative attribute that is not described by existence or non-existence. For the deniers, only attributes of meanings exist, no states. For the affirmers, attributes are divided into three categories: psychic (nafsiyya), meaningful (ma‘nawiyya), and meanings (ma‘ānī). The reason for this exclusive division is that anything actualized is either actualized by virtue of itself (which is the 'existent', meaning the actual attribute like knowledge or power) or by virtue of something else (which is the 'state'). The footnote clarifies that al-mawjud refers to the existing description like knowledge and power.

الصفات النفسية
الصفات المعنوية
صفات المعاني

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that all Ash'aris accept the reality of states, but al-Ash'ari himself denied them.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that al-Ash'ari and many investigators denied states, while later figures like al-Qāḍī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn affirmed them.

B) Those who affirm states
C) Both groups
D) Neither group

Key Takeaway
The acceptance or rejection of states fundamentally changes how divine attributes are categorized, with affirmers using a threefold division based on whether an attribute is actualized by itself or by another.

Ma'nawiyya Attributes and the Concept of al-Ḥāl
Sanusi defines ma'nawiyya attributes and introduces the concept of ḥāl as an intermediary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of ma'nawiyya attributes, their relationship to attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī), and the concept of a state (ḥāl) as an intermediary between existence and non-existence.

Core Idea
Ma'nawiyya attributes are caused by meanings; the state is the middle between existence and non-existence.

Sanusi begins by clarifying how we speak about God's attributes. He distinguishes between attributes that are themselves meanings (like power, knowledge) and the qualitative attributes resulting from them (like being powerful, being knowing). This leads to a key concept in kalām: the notion of a 'state' (ḥāl) that is neither existent nor non-existent. In this lesson, we explore this foundational distinction and the idea of an intermediary category.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic carefully along with the literal translation. Notice how Sanusi defines ma'nawiyya and ṣifāt al-maʿānī.
The example of power and being powerful is central.
2
Identify the causal relationship
Understand that ma'nawiyya attributes are caused by meanings that subsist in the essence. The causes are described as not qualified by existence or non-existence.
The causes are 'attributes of meanings' (ṣifāt al-maʿānī).
3
Grasp the concept of al-wāsiṭa
Note the phrase 'on the view affirming the intermediary between existence and non-existence.' This is the core of the concept of ḥāl.
The intermediary is what will later be called a 'state' (ḥāl).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأجل ملازمتها معانيَ أُخَرَ هي عِلَلٌ لِـ: صفاتٍ معنويةٍ، وأحوالٍ معنويةٍ، نُسِبَتْ إلى المعاني التي هي عِلَلُها؛ ككونه قادراً عليَّه القدرةَ، وككونه عالماً علَّتُه العلمُ، وهكذا إلى آخرِها، وتُسمَّى هذهِ العِلَلُ الملازمةُ للمعنويةِ: صفاتِ المعاني، فالمعنويةُ: صفات ثابتة للذاتِ مُعلَّلَةٌ بمعنى قائم بالذاتِ، وعلَلُها صفات لا تتصف بوجود ولا عدم، موجودة قائمة بالذاتِ مُوجِبةٌ لها حُكماً؛ وهو تلك الصفة المعنوية. هذا كله على القول بصحة الواسطة بين الوجود والعدم. وأما على القولِ بنفيها: فليسَ ثَمَّ إلا الذات وصفات المعاني الوجودية، ولا معنى عندهم لكونه عالماً أو قادراً إلا قيام العلم والقدرةِ بهِ، فلا حالَ عند هؤلاء لا معنويةً ولا نفسيَّةً. وبالجملة: فالمتكلمون على فريقين: فريق ينفي الحال، وفريق يُثْبِتُها. وحقيقةُ الحالِ: صفةٌ إثباتٌ لا تتصف بالوجود ولا بالعدم. فالقائلون بنفي الأحوالِ؛ كالشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري وكثيرٍ من المحققين: ليس عندهم من الصفاتِ إلا صفات المعاني. والقائلون بثبوتِ الحالِ؛ كالقاضي وإمام الحرمين: يقسمونَ الصفات ثلاثة أقسام: نفسيَّةٌ، ومعنويةٌ، ومعانٍ، ووجه الحصرِ: أنَّ المتحقَّقَ إما أن يتحقَّقَ باعتبارِ نفسِهِ، أو باعتبار غيرِه، الأول: الموجود (الوصف الموجود؛ كالعلم والقدرة مثلاً)، والثاني: الحالُ؛ وهو إما أنْ يكونَ الغيرُ الذي تحقَّقَ به ذاتَ موصوفِهِ (أي حقيقة، سواء كانت ذاتاً أو صفة)، أو معنى يقومُ بموصوفِهِ، الأَوَّلُ: الحالُ النفسيَّةُ والثاني: الحالُ المعنويةُ.
Because they are accompanied by other meanings that are causes for: qualitative attributes (ṣifāt maʿnawiyya) and qualitative states (aḥwāl maʿnawiyya), which are attributed to the meanings that are their causes; such as His being powerful by virtue of power, and His being knowing by virtue of knowledge, and so on to the rest of them. And these causes that are concomitant with the qualitative are called attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī). So the qualitative (al-maʿnawiyya) are attributes established for the essence, caused by a meaning subsisting in the essence, and their causes are attributes that are not qualified by existence or non-existence, existing, subsisting in the essence, necessitating for them a judgment; which is that qualitative attribute. All this is on the view affirming the intermediary (al-wāsiṭa) between existence and non-existence. But on the view denying it: there is nothing except the essence and the existential attributes of meanings, and there is no meaning for them of His being knowing or powerful except the subsistence of knowledge and power in Him, so there is no state (ḥāl) for these people, neither qualitative nor essential (nafsiyya). In summary: the theologians are two groups: a group denying the state (al-ḥāl), and a group affirming it. The reality of the state is an affirmative attribute not qualified by existence or non-existence. Those who deny states, such as Shaykh Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ashʿarī and many of the investigators: they have none of the attributes except the attributes of meanings. Those who affirm the state, such as al-Qāḍī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn: they divide the attributes into three divisions: essential (nafsiyya), qualitative (maʿnawiyya), and meanings (maʿānī). And the reason for the enumeration is: that what is realized either is realized by consideration of itself, or by consideration of other than itself. The first: the existent (i.e., the existing attribute, like knowledge and power for example). The second: the state; and it is either that the other by which it is realized is the essence of its described (i.e., the reality, whether it is an essence or an attribute), or a meaning subsisting in its described. The first: the essential state (al-ḥāl al-nafsiyya), and the second: the qualitative state (al-ḥāl al-maʿnawiyya).
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the relationship between qualitative attributes (ṣifāt maʿnawiyya) and attributes of meaning (ṣifāt al-maʿānī). The author begins by stating that qualitative attributes are accompanied by other meanings that serve as causes for them. For example, God's being powerful is attributed to the power (al-qudra) that subsists in His essence as a meaning. These causal meanings are called 'attributes of meanings'. The qualitative attributes are established for the essence but are caused by a meaning in the essence. The causes themselves are described as not having existence or non-existence; they are intermediaries (wāsiṭa) between existence and non-existence. Then the author discusses two theological positions: the first affirms this intermediary (the 'state' or ḥāl) between existence and non-existence, while the second denies it. Those who deny states (like al-Ashʿarī) hold that there are only the essence and the existential attributes of meanings; no state exists. Those who affirm states (like al-Qāḍī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn) divide attributes into three categories: essential (nafsiyya), qualitative (maʿnawiyya), and meanings (maʿānī). The passage then explains the logic of this threefold division: whatever is realized is either realized by itself (the existent attribute) or by another (the state). The state is further divided into essential state (when the other is the essence itself) and qualitative state (when the other is a meaning subsisting in the essence).

Key Terms
صفة معنوية
صفة المعنى
حال
واسطة بين الوجود والعدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ma'nawiyya attributes are the same as attributes of meanings.
Correction: Ma'nawiyya are caused by attributes of meanings; they are distinct.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are 'attributes of meanings' (ṣifāt al-maʿānī)?
A) The same as ma'nawiyya attributes
B) The causes that are concomitant with ma'nawiyya
C) Attributes that are not caused by anything
D) The essence itself

Key Takeaway
Ma'nawiyya attributes are caused by attributes of meanings, which are intermediary realities not fully existent nor non-existent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the attributes of God like power and knowledge are only intermediary states—neither fully existent nor non-existent—how does that affect your confidence that you truly know Him through these attributes? Do you rely more on intellectual formulas or on direct experience of His acts? What would it take for you to move from theological abstraction to living certainty?
?
The passage says that the maʿnawiyya attributes are 'caused' by meanings. When you call God 'All-Powerful,' are you merely repeating a definition, or do you sense that His power is a real cause behind every event in your life? Examine your heart: is your faith in God's attributes a theoretical framework or a transformative reality? If it's the former, what step will you take today to make it the latter?

The Two Views on Aḥwāl and the Threefold Division of Attributes
Sanusi contrasts the two views on aḥwāl and explains the threefold classification of attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two theological positions regarding states (aḥwāl) and the threefold division of attributes proposed by those who affirm them.

Core Idea
Theologians split on states: some deny them, others affirm and classify attributes into three.

After introducing the concept of a state as an intermediary, Sanusi now presents the two major positions in kalām: those who reject states altogether (like al-Ashʿarī) and those who accept them and thereby divide attributes into three categories. This lesson unpacks that dispute and the logic behind the threefold classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups
Read the passage and note the two groups: those who deny states and those who affirm states. Who are the representatives?
Al-Ashʿarī denies states; al-Qāḍī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn affirm them.
2
Understand the position of deniers
They hold that there are only the essence and the existential attributes of meanings. No intermediate reality exists.
For them, 'God is knowing' simply means knowledge subsists in Him.
3
Understand the threefold division
Affirmers divide attributes into essential (nafsiyya), qualitative (maʿnawiyya), and meanings (maʿānī). Grasp the reasoning: what is realized either by itself or by another, and the other can be the essence itself or a meaning subsisting in it.
Essential state arises from the essence; qualitative state arises from a meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Because they are accompanied by other meanings that are causes for: qualitative attributes (ṣifāt maʿnawiyya) and qualitative states (aḥwāl maʿnawiyya), which are attributed to the meanings that are their causes; such as His being powerful by virtue of power, and His being knowing by virtue of knowledge, and so on to the rest of them. ?

?

?

Examine your heart: do you truly rely on Allah as the Self-Sufficient, or do you lean on created means as if they are independent? This lesson calls you to purge hidden shirk from your dependence.

Later Scholars Add Three Categories
Sanusi reports a sixfold classification of attributes by later theologians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that later theologians expanded the threefold classification of divine attributes to six by adding negative, active, and comprehensive attributes.

Core Idea
The sixfold classification includes negative, active, and comprehensive categories.

Sanusi briefly reports a development in the classification of divine attributes. Some later theologians did not stop at the three main sets (essential, qualitative, and relational) but added three more: negative, active, and comprehensive. This lesson explores that expansion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Note that it describes a sixfold classification.
The passage is short, so take time to understand each term.
2
Identify the six categories
Recognize that the original three categories are implied (essential, qualitative, meanings) and the three added are explicitly named: negative, active, comprehensive.
The term 'salbiyya' means negation, 'fiʿliyya' relates to actions, and 'jāmiʿa' unites all.
3
Consider the diversity of definitions
The passage states that later scholars have various expressions for defining these divisions. Reflect on why different definitions might arise.
This indicates that the classification is not monolithic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجعلَها بعضُ المتأخّرينَ ستة أقسامٍ، ضمَّ إلى هذه الثلاثةِ ثلاثةً أُخَر؛ وهي السلبيةُ، والفعليةُ، والجامعةُ لجميع الأقسامِ، ولهم في تعريف هذه الأقسام عباراتٌ.
And some of the later [scholars] made them six divisions, adding to these three another three: namely the negative (salbiyya), the active (fiʿliyya), and the comprehensive (jāmiʿa) of all divisions. And they have various expressions regarding the definition of these divisions.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage is a brief report on a later development in the classification of divine attributes. The author notes that some later theologians expanded the earlier threefold division (essential, qualitative, and meanings) to six divisions by adding three more: negative attributes (al-ṣifāt al-salbiyya), active attributes (al-ṣifāt al-fiʿliyya), and a comprehensive category that includes all divisions (al-ṣifāt al-jāmiʿa li-jamīʿ al-aqsām). The passage mentions that these scholars have various definitions for these divisions, implying that there is some diversity of opinion on the precise meaning of each category.

Key Terms

صفات فعلية
الصفات الجامعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The sixfold classification is universally accepted by all later scholars.
Correction: The passage says 'some' later scholars made this division, indicating it is not universal.

Checkpoint

B) Necessary, possible, and impossible
C) Essential, qualitative, and relational
D) Anthropomorphic, metaphorical, and literal

Key Takeaway
Later theologians expanded the classification of divine attributes from three to six by adding negative, active, and comprehensive categories.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Negative Attributes: Definition and Nuances
Sanusi defines negative attributes and discusses permissible negations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of negative attributes in Islamic theology, including the verified view and the concept of permissible negations.

Core Idea
Negative attributes are the negation of what cannot be said about God.

Sanusi begins by clarifying what negative attributes are. He first reports a common definition, then presents a more precise, verified one. He also introduces the subtle idea that some negations may be 'permissible' in God's right, which leads to the concept of temporality in certain divine acts like pardon.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully focusing on the definition and examples. Notice the distinction between the common and verified definitions.
The ellipsis '... إلى آخرِهِ' indicates an omission; the core meaning is clear.
2
Identify the two definitions
Find the common definition ('قالوا: إنها عبارة عن كل ما يمتنع...') and the verified definition ('والتحقيق: أنها عبارة عن نفي كل ما يمتنع'). Understand the difference.
The verified view refines the common one: it is not simply 'what is impossible to attribute', but the 'negation of all that is impossible'.
3
Understand permissible negations
Note that some negations are not absolute but permissible (جائزة). The example of God's pardon after an offense shows that these are expressed as temporal (حادثة).
This nuance prevents misunderstanding that all negative attributes are mere negations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الصفات السلبية فقالوا: إنّها عبارةٌ عن كل ما يمتنع أن يوصف به البارئ جل وعلا. والتحقيق: أنَّها عبارةٌ عن نفي كل ما يمتنع ... إلى آخرِهِ؛ وذلك كسلب الشريك والجسميَّةِ والعرضيَّةِ ونحو ذلك، وقد تكون بعضُ السلوبِ جائزةً في حقِّهِ تعالى، ومنهم مَنْ يُعبر عنها بالحدوثِ (أي بالمشتق منه؛ بأن يقول: هذه الصفات حادثة)؛ وذلك كعفوه تعالى وحلمِهِ بعدَ الجنايةِ؛ فإنَّهُ عبارةٌ عن إسقاط العقوبة معَ تحقُّقِ الجنايةِ. وأمَّا الصفات النفسيَّةُ فقيل: إنَّها عبارة عن كلِّ حالٍ ثبَتَتْ للذاتِ غير مُعلَّلة.
As for the negative attributes (al-ṣifāt al-salbiyya), they said: they are an expression for everything that it is impossible to describe the Creator, may He be exalted, with. And the verified [view] is that they are an expression for the negation of everything that is impossible... to the end of that; such as the negation of a partner, corporeality, accidentality, and the like. And some negations may be permissible with respect to Him, may He be exalted; and among them are those who express them by 'temporality' (al-ḥudūth) (i.e., by the derived term; such as saying: these attributes are temporal); such as His pardon, may He be exalted, and His forbearance after the offense; for it is an expression for the dropping of the punishment while the offense is realized. As for the essential attributes (al-ṣifāt al-nafsiyya), it is said: they are an expression for every state (ḥāl) that is established for the essence without being caused.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage provides definitions for two categories of attributes: negative (salbiyya) and essential (nafsiyya). For negative attributes, the author first reports the common definition: they are everything that it is impossible to attribute to God. Then he gives the more precise, verified definition: they are the negation of everything impossible (i.e., the negation of what cannot be said of God). Examples include negating a partner, corporeality, and accidentality. The author also notes that some negations can be 'permissible' (jāʾiza) in God's right, meaning they are not absolute negations but indicate a possible event. Some scholars express these permissible negations as 'temporality' (ḥudūth), meaning that the attribute is temporal, not eternal. An example is God's pardon after an offense—this is expressed as the dropping of punishment while the offense is realized, which implies a temporal aspect. For the essential attributes, the definition given is: every state (ḥāl) that is established for the essence without being caused (by a meaning). This means these attributes are not dependent on any cause; they are intrinsic to the essence.

Key Terms
صفات سلبية
سلب
جائزة
حداثة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All negative attributes are mere negations of imperfections in God.
Correction: Some negative attributes are 'permissible' and imply temporality, as in the case of God's pardon after an offense.

Checkpoint
According to the verified definition, what are negative attributes?
A) Attributes that negate all imperfections from God
B) The negation of everything that it is impossible to attribute to God
C) Attributes that are temporal
D) Attributes that are not caused

Key Takeaway
Negative attributes are the negation of all that is impossible for God, with some negations being permissible and implying temporality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage teaches that God's pardon is a 'permissible negation' that implies temporality—it drops punishment only after the offense. When you sin, do you truly believe that God's forgiveness is a real event that occurs in time relative to your action? How does that belief affect the urgency of your repentance?
?
Sanusi says some negations are 'permissible' and not absolute. This means your understanding of God must allow for actions that have a temporal aspect. Are there areas of your life where you secretly expect God to act according to your timeline or conditions, rather than His? Will you surrender that expectation today?
?
If negative attributes are about negating what cannot be said of God, the inclusion of permissible negations shows that theology is not just negative but also acknowledges God's real interactions with creation. How does this nuance change the way you speak about God in your daily conversations? Can you commit to avoiding simplistic descriptions that limit His transcendence?

Essential Attributes: Definition and Key Features
Sanusi defines essential attributes (ṣifāt nafsiyya).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of essential attributes (ṣifāt nafsiyya) and their key feature: they are states established for the essence without being caused.

Core Idea
Essential attributes are uncaused states intrinsic to the divine essence.

Sanusi now turns to essential attributes. He provides a concise definition: they are states (ḥāl) that are established for the essence without being caused. This means they are not dependent on any external cause or meaning; they are purely intrinsic to God's essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic sentence
Read the Arabic sentence defining essential attributes. Notice the key terms: 'حال' (state), 'ثَبتَت للذات' (established for the essence), and 'غير مُعلَّلة' (without being caused).
The phrase 'فقيل' indicates this is one reported definition.
2
Understand the concept of 'state'
A 'state' (ḥāl) in kalam is an attribute that is not a separate entity but is nevertheless real. Here it is established for the essence itself.
Essential attributes are not accidental; they are co-eternal with the essence.
3
Focus on 'غير مُعلَّلة'
The phrase 'without being caused' means these attributes have no cause or ground. They are not derived from anything else; they are self-subsisting attributes of God.
This distinguishes them from other attributes that may have a cause (like knowledge caused by omniscience).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الصفات السلبية فقالوا: إنّها عبارةٌ عن كل ما يمتنع أن يوصف به البارئ جل وعلا. والتحقيق: أنَّها عبارةٌ عن نفي كل ما يمتنع ... إلى آخرِهِ؛ وذلك كسلب الشريك والجسميَّةِ والعرضيَّةِ ونحو ذلك، وقد تكون بعضُ السلوبِ جائزةً في حقِّهِ تعالى، ومنهم مَنْ يُعبر عنها بالحدوثِ (أي بالمشتق منه؛ بأن يقول: هذه الصفات حادثة)؛ وذلك كعفوه تعالى وحلمِهِ بعدَ الجنايةِ؛ فإنَّهُ عبارةٌ عن إسقاط العقوبة معَ تحقُّقِ الجنايةِ. وأمَّا الصفات النفسيَّةُ فقيل: إنَّها عبارة عن كلِّ حالٍ ثبَتَتْ للذاتِ غير مُعلَّلة.
As for the negative attributes (al-ṣifāt al-salbiyya), they said: they are an expression for everything that it is impossible to describe the Creator, may He be exalted, with. And the verified [view] is that they are an expression for the negation of everything that is impossible... to the end of that; such as the negation of a partner, corporeality, accidentality, and the like. And some negations may be permissible with respect to Him, may He be exalted; and among them are those who express them by 'temporality' (al-ḥudūth) (i.e., by the derived term; such as saying: these attributes are temporal); such as His pardon, may He be exalted, and His forbearance after the offense; for it is an expression for the dropping of the punishment while the offense is realized. As for the essential attributes (al-ṣifāt al-nafsiyya), it is said: they are an expression for every state (ḥāl) that is established for the essence without being caused.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage provides definitions for two categories of attributes: negative (salbiyya) and essential (nafsiyya). For negative attributes, the author first reports the common definition: they are everything that it is impossible to attribute to God. Then he gives the more precise, verified definition: they are the negation of everything impossible (i.e., the negation of what cannot be said of God). Examples include negating a partner, corporeality, and accidentality. The author also notes that some negations can be 'permissible' (jāʾiza) in God's right, meaning they are not absolute negations but indicate a possible event. Some scholars express these permissible negations as 'temporality' (ḥudūth), meaning that the attribute is temporal, not eternal. An example is God's pardon after an offense—this is expressed as the dropping of punishment while the offense is realized, which implies a temporal aspect. For the essential attributes, the definition given is: every state (ḥāl) that is established for the essence without being caused (by a meaning). This means these attributes are not dependent on any cause; they are intrinsic to the essence.

Key Terms
صفات نفسية
حال
غير معللة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Essential attributes are caused by some meaning or external factor.
Correction: The definition explicitly states they are 'غير معللة' (uncaused), meaning they are intrinsic and not dependent on any cause.

Checkpoint
According to the definition, what does the phrase 'غير معللة' indicate about essential attributes?
A) They are temporal
B) They are not caused
C) They are contingent
D) They are negations

Key Takeaway
Essential attributes are uncaused states that are established for the divine essence itself.

Three Definitions of Essential Attributes (al-Ṣifāt al-Nafsiyya)
Sanusi gives three definitions of essential attributes and discusses their true nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three definitions of essential attributes given by Sanusi and the verified view that they reduce to negative attributes.

Core Idea
Essential attributes are not separate; they reduce to negation or are unknowable.

Sanusi begins by clarifying what essential attributes are, presenting three definitions from the tradition. After critiquing a common example, he provides the verified view that these attributes ultimately reduce to negative attributes. This lesson unpacks each definition and the key conclusions about their nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the three definitions and the critical remark about the example.
The passage uses technical terms like 'ḥāl' and 'mu‘allala'.
2
Identify the three definitions
Find each definition and note how they differ: (1) state without cause, (2) attribute without additional meaning, (3) attribute whose removal is inconceivable while essence remains.
All three reduce to one thing according to Sanusi.
3
Understand the critique
Sanusi questions the common example (being necessarily existent, eternal, everlasting). Consider why this example might be problematic.
The verified view is that these attributes reduce to negative attributes.
4
Grasp the final claim
The verifying scholars hold that essential attributes are not known from kalām books; knowing them would mean knowing the essence, which only God knows.
This points to the limits of human knowledge of God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا الصفات النفسيَّةُ فقيل : إنَّها عبارة عن كلِّ حالٍ ثبَتَتْ للذاتِ غير مُعلَّلة وقيل : هي كلُّ صفةِ إثباتِ للذاتِ مِنْ غيرِ معنی زائد على الذاتِ وقيل : هي كلُّ صفةٍ ثبوتية زائدة على الذاتِ لا يصح توهم انتفائها مع بقاء الذاتِ الموصوفة بها ، وهي في الحقيقة راجعة إلى شيء واحد . ويمثلون النفسيةَ : بكونِهِ واجب الوجودِ أزليّاً أبدياً ، وفيه نظر (۱) والتحقيق : رجوعُ هذه الصفاتِ إلى السلب ، وقد سبق ذلك (٢) ، والمحققون يرون أنَّ الصفاتِ النفسية لم يُعرَف منها في كُتُب الكلام ، ولو عرفناها لكُنَّا قد عرفنا الذات ، ولا يعرفُ الله إلا الله
As for the essential attributes (al-ṣifāt al-nafsiyya), it was said: they are every state that is established for the essence without a cause. And it was said: they are every attribute of affirmation for the essence without an additional meaning over the essence. And it was said: they are every affirmative attribute additional to the essence such that it is not valid to suppose its removal while the described essence remains, and they in reality refer to one thing. They exemplify the essential attributes by His being necessarily existent, eternal, everlasting, and there is a consideration in this. The verified view: these attributes reduce to negative (attributes), and this has preceded. The verifying scholars hold that the essential attributes are not known from the books of kalām; if we knew them, we would have known the essence, and God does not know (anyone) except God.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage provides three definitions of essential attributes (al-ṣifāt al-nafsiyya): (1) a state established for the essence without a cause (ghayr mu‘allala); (2) an attribute of affirmation for the essence without an additional meaning over the essence; (3) an affirmative attribute additional to the essence whose removal cannot be imagined while the essence remains. The passage notes that all three reduce to one thing. The example given (being necessarily existent, eternal, everlasting) is questionable. The verified view is that these attributes reduce to negative attributes. The verifying scholars hold that essential attributes are not known in the books of kalām; if we knew them, we would know the essence, but only God knows God.

Key Terms
الصفات النفسية
الحال
معللة
واجب الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Essential attributes are separate qualities added to the divine essence.
Correction: The verified view is that they reduce to negative attributes (denial of imperfections) and are ultimately unknowable; they are not separate additions.

Checkpoint
What is the verified view (al-taḥqīq) regarding essential attributes?
A) They are all unknowable
B) They reduce to negative attributes
C) They are additional to the essence
D) They are eternal and everlasting

Key Takeaway
The essential attributes, though defined in three ways, ultimately reduce to negative attributes and remain beyond full human comprehension.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The passage says the essential attributes are not known from the books of kalām. Does this disappoint you? Are you striving to know God through positive descriptions that He has not given? What would it look like to worship a God whose essence you cannot fully grasp, trusting Him with the unknowable?

Definition of Meaningful Attributes (Ṣifāt Ma'nawiyya)
Sanusi defines meaningful attributes with two formulations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of meaningful attributes as states caused by a meaning subsisting in the essence, and how they differ from essential attributes.

Core Idea
Meaningful attributes are caused states, not uncaused essences.

In this passage, Sanusi defines a key category of divine attributes: the ṣifāt maʿnawiyya. These are attributes that exist as states arising from a meaning within the essence itself. The passage gives two complementary definitions to clarify this concept.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to get a feel for the phrasing. Note the two definitions introduced by 'هي عبارة عن' and 'وقيل'.
The text uses technical terms like 'معللة' and 'قائم بالذات'—look for their English meanings.
2
Identify the two definitions
The passage presents two definitions of meaningful attributes. Find each one and observe how they differ in wording: one speaks of 'state established for the essence', the other of 'attribute necessary for the essence'.
Both definitions share the key idea: the attribute is caused by a meaning in the essence.
3
Understand the causal relationship
Focus on the term 'معللة' (caused). Meaningful attributes are not simply inherent like essential attributes; they depend on a meaning (maʿnā) that subsists in the essence. This causal link is what distinguishes them.
Contrast with ṣifāt dhātiyya (essential attributes) which are not caused.
4
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Some may think meaningful attributes are separate from the essence. The passage clarifies they are states caused by a meaning within the essence, not external additions.
This connects to the bigger picture of divine simplicity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الصفات المعنوية : فهي عبارة عن كلِّ حالٍ ثبَتَتْ للذاتِ مُعلَّلَةٌ بمعنى قائم بالذات وقيل : هي كلُّ صفة لازمة للذات لأجل معنى قائم بالذات
As for the meaningful attributes (al-ṣifāt al-ma‘nawiyya), they are expressions for every state that is established for the essence, caused by a meaning subsisting in the essence. And it was said: they are every attribute necessary for the essence due to a meaning subsisting in the essence.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage defines meaningful attributes (al-ṣifāt al-ma‘nawiyya) with two related definitions. The first: they are every state that is established for the essence and is caused (mu‘allala) by a meaning subsisting in the essence. The second: they are every attribute that is necessary for the essence because of a meaning subsisting in the essence. This contrasts with essential attributes, which are uncaused.

Understanding Psychic Attributes
Sanusi defines psychic attributes and discusses their reality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two definitions of psychic attributes in kalam and why the verified position is that they return to negation and are unknowable in their inner reality.

Core Idea
Psychic attributes affirm the essence yet reduce to negation and are beyond human knowledge.

This passage from Sanusi’s Umm al-Barahin addresses the subtle concept of psychic attributes (الصفات النفسية). These are attributes so intrinsic to the divine essence that scholars debate whether they are additional to it or merely affirm it without extra meaning. Sanusi presents two definitions, raises a problem with the standard example, and then settles on the position that these attributes ultimately return to negation and are unknowable in their true reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation to grasp the overall flow.
This is a dense conceptual text; focus on the main ideas first.
2
Identify the two definitions
Notice that Sanusi gives two definitions of psychic attributes. The first says they are affirmation without additional meaning; the second says they are additional yet inseparable from the essence.
Both definitions attempt to describe how these attributes relate to the divine essence.
3
Examine the example and the author's note
The example given (necessary existence, eternity) is common, but the author remarks that there is ‘consideration’ (نظر) in it. Think about why this example might be problematic.
This prepares for the verification that the attributes return to negation.
4
Understand the verification and the unknowability claim
The verified position is that these attributes reduce to negation. Moreover, the scholars say that their true reality is not known in kalam books; if we knew them, we would know the essence, but none knows Allah except Allah.
This highlights a limit of theological inquiry.
5
Distinguish knowledge of definition from knowledge of reality
The footnote clarifies that we can know psychic attributes by definition (رسم), but not by inner reality (كنه). Reflect on how this distinction preserves both divine transcendence and meaningful discourse.
Imam al-Razi’s quote reinforces that Allah’s existence is utterly distinct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيل : هي كلُّ صفةِ إثباتِ للذاتِ مِنْ غيرِ معنی زائد على الذاتِ وقيل : هي كلُّ صفةٍ ثبوتية زائدة على الذاتِ لا يصح توهم انتفائها مع بقاء الذاتِ الموصوفة بها ، وهي في الحقيقة راجعة إلى شيء واحد . ويمثلون النفسيةَ : بكونِهِ واجب الوجودِ أزليّاً أبدياً ، وفيه نظر (۱) والتحقيق : رجوعُ هذه الصفاتِ إلى السلب ، وقد سبق ذلك (٢) ، والمحققون يرون أنَّ الصفاتِ النفسية لم يُعرَف منها في كُتُب الكلام ، ولو عرفناها لكُنَّا قد عرفنا الذات ، ولا يعرفُ الله إلا الله . شيء (۳) أي : معرفة كُنه وحقيقة ، لا معرفة رسم ، وإلا فهي معروفة مسندة في كتب علم الكلام . عكاري » ( ق ١٤٧ ) ، فلا يبعد أن تكون معرفة حقيقة وجوده تعالى منتفية عنا ، مع جزمنا بوجوده ، قال الإمام الرازي في « الإشارة » ( ص ٧٦ ) : ( وجوده تعالی مباين لوجود الخلق من جميع الوجوه ، وإذا قيل : البارئ يشارك الممكنات في الوجود .. فاعلم : أنه لا مشاركة إلا في الاسم ، وهذا هو مذهب شيخنا أبي الحسن ) .
And it was said: It is every attribute of affirmation for the essence without an additional meaning over the essence. And it was said: It is every positive attribute additional to the essence that it is not valid to imagine its removal while the essence that is described by it remains, and in reality they return to one thing. And they exemplify the psychic attribute by His being necessary of existence, eternal, everlasting, and there is consideration in it (1). And the verification: the return of these attributes to negation, and that has preceded (2). And the verifiers hold that the psychic attributes are not known in the books of kalam, and if we knew them we would have known the essence, and none knows Allah except Allah. Something (3). i.e., knowledge of the inner reality and essence, not knowledge of definition. Otherwise it is known and documented in the books of kalam. Imam al-Razi said in al-Ishara (p. 76): 'His existence is distinct from the existence of creation in all respects, and if it is said that the Creator shares existence with possibles... know that there is no sharing except in name, and this is the doctrine of our teacher Abu al-Hasan.'
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage defines and discusses psychic attributes (الصفات النفسية). Two definitions are presented: first, attributes that affirm the essence without any additional meaning; second, positive attributes whose removal cannot be imagined while the essence remains, though they reduce to one reality. An example is given (necessary existence, eternity), but the author notes there is consideration (نظر) in this example. The verified position is that these attributes return to negation (سلب), which has been mentioned earlier. Imam al-Razi is quoted to emphasize that Allah's existence is utterly distinct from creation; any sharing is only in name.

Meaningful Attributes Defined
Sanusi defines meaningful attributes with two definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of meaningful attributes as states caused by a meaning subsisting in the divine essence.

Core Idea
Meaningful attributes are caused by a meaning in the essence, not identical to it.

In this brief but foundational passage, Sanusi defines a key category of divine attributes: the meaningful attributes (الصفات المعنوية). These attributes are not mere concepts but are rooted in a real, distinct meaning within the divine essence. We'll explore two definitions that highlight their causal relationship with the essence, setting the stage for understanding how attributes relate to God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the two definitions are connected by 'وقيل' (and it was said).
The passage uses technical terms like 'حال', 'معللة', and 'معنى'.
2
Identify the two definitions
The first definition describes meaningful attributes as a 'state' (حال) caused by a meaning. The second defines them as 'attributes necessary for the essence' because of a meaning. Spot the difference in wording.
3
Understand the key distinction
Both definitions emphasize that these attributes are not identical to the essence; they are caused (معللة) by a meaning that subsists in the essence. This distinguishes them from attributes of the essence itself.
The phrase 'بمعنى قائم بالذات' (by a meaning subsisting in the essence) is crucial.
4
Reflect on the importance

This connects to broader debates about divine simplicity and attribute realism.

Source Text

The second defines them as attributes necessarily attached to the essence because of a meaning subsisting in the essence. Both definitions emphasize that these attributes are not identical to the essence but arise from a distinct meaning in the essence.

Definition of Attributes of Meanings and Their Relation to Meaningful Attributes
Sanusi defines attributes of meanings and their necessary connection to meaningful attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of attributes of meanings (صفات المعاني) and their necessary causal relationship with meaningful attributes (الصفات المعنوية) according to Ahl al-Sunnah.

Core Idea
Attributes of meanings are the cause; meaningful attributes are the effect.

Sanusi now turns from the division of attributes to a precise definition of one of those categories: attributes of meanings. He provides two complementary definitions and then clarifies how these relate to the meaningful attributes. This lesson establishes the cause-effect framework that underpins the Sunni position on divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the definitions of attributes of meanings
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the two definitions given: first as attributes necessitating a judgment, second as meanings necessitating states.
The second definition is introduced with 'and it was said'.
2
Compare the two definitions
Observe that both definitions emphasize necessity—these attributes are not static but actively necessitate something in the described thing.
3
Understand the relationship: necessary connection of cause and effect
The passage explicitly states that between attributes of meanings and meaningful attributes there is a necessary connection, like cause and effect. This means the former bring about the latter.
This is the position of Ahl al-Sunnah.
4
Reflect on why this distinction matters
Consider how this causal link preserves the reality and efficacy of divine attributes without conflating distinct categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما صفات المعاني : فهي عبارةٌ عن كل صفة قائمة بموصوف موجبة له حكماً وقيل : هي المعاني الموجبة للأحوالِ . فبين المعاني والمعنويَّةِ تلازم عند أهلِ السنَّةِ تلازم العلَّة ومعلولها .
And as for the attributes of meanings (صفات المعاني): they are expressions for every attribute subsisting in a described thing that necessitates a judgment for it. And it was said: They are the meanings that necessitate the states. And between the attributes of meanings and the meaningful attributes there is a necessary connection according to the People of the Sunnah, the necessary connection of cause and effect.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage defines attributes of meanings (صفات المعاني) and clarifies their relationship with meaningful attributes (الصفات المعنوية). Two definitions are given: first, they are attributes subsisting in a described thing that necessitate a judgment; second, they are the meanings that necessitate the states (الأحوال). The passage then states that according to Ahl al-Sunnah, there is a necessary connection (تلازم) between these two categories, like the connection between cause and effect. In other words, the attributes of meanings are the causes that produce the meaningful attributes.

Key Terms

التلازم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think attributes of meanings and meaningful attributes are the same or have no relationship.
Correction: They are distinct categories with a necessary causal relationship: attributes of meanings are the cause, meaningful attributes are the effect.

Checkpoint

A) They are identical
B) No relationship
C) Necessary connection of cause and effect
D) They are opposites

Key Takeaway
Attributes of meanings are the causal grounds for the meaningful attributes, linked necessarily as cause and effect.

?

?
Do you realize that your knowledge of God as described by these attributes is not just theoretical but grounded in real, subsisting realities? How does that compel you to respond to Him in worship and obedience today?
